  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_865bcb75-8fc5-4e2f-9db3-4562be2cbe3a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText6380414707575925532" style="display:none"><i>A dark and tender post-apocalyptic love story set in the aftermath of a bloody war.</i><br /><br />In a city where humans and Darklings are now separated by a high wall and tensions between the two races still simmer after a terrible war, sixteen-year-old Ash Fisher, a half-blood Darkling, and Natalie Buchanan, a human and the daughter of the Emissary, meet and do the unthinkable—they fall in love. Bonded by a mysterious connection that causes Ash’s long-dormant heart to beat, Ash and Natalie first deny and then struggle to fight their forbidden feelings for each other, knowing if they’re caught, they’ll be executed—but their feelings are too strong.<br /><br />When Ash and Natalie then find themselves at the center of a deadly conspiracy that threatens to pull the humans and Darklings back into war, they must make hard choices that could result in both their deaths.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_457943096" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457943096" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/457943096?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer457943096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3387720618661238208">I think I've permanently damaged my eyeballs from rolling them so much.<br/><br/>It seems like I can't get into anything lately, I've read so many new releases to about chapter five and then I have to give up. The only good thing about this book is that my expectations were low as they now are with every book marketed as a dystopia - which, to be honest, this just isn't a dystopia in any sense of the word. For one, it's mostly a love story, but I'm not too upset about that because I received fair warning </span>
  <span id="freeText3387720618661238208" style="display:none">I think I've permanently damaged my eyeballs from rolling them so much.<br><br>It seems like I can't get into anything lately, I've read so many new releases to about chapter five and then I have to give up. The only good thing about this book is that my expectations were low as they now are with every book marketed as a dystopia - which, to be honest, this just isn't a dystopia in any sense of the word. For one, it's mostly a love story, but I'm not too upset about that because I received fair warning of it in the GR description - I just had my fingers crossed that it wouldn't be another annoying, cliche, insta-love story (apparently, this doesn't actually work). <br><br>For another, it's more of a dark fantasy/urban fantasy than a dystopia - the world reminded me somewhat of Ixion in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9433912.Burn_Bright__Night_Creatures___1_" title="Burn Bright (Night Creatures, #1) by Marianne de Pierres" rel="nofollow noopener">Burn Bright</a> - with the only hints of the latter being in the similarities between this world and Cold War Berlin where the city is split by a wall that separates humans and darklings (vampires, basically). Apart from this rather intriguing world, everything else from the characters to the plot to the love story were lacking in originality. I think I even recognise some scenes from popular series like Harry Potter and Twilight.<br><br><i>"You don't want to be seen with her sort, she's one of the Rise kids," he says to Natalie. "I'll set you up with the right type of people to know."<br>"I can make my own mind up about who the 'right type of people' are," Natalie snaps."I'm already getting a pretty good idea of who I want to avoid."</i><br><br><b>I seen this before!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380397946ra/768503.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380397946ra/768504.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380397946ra/768505.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380397946ra/768506.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>And the love story makes me cringe, it's so... <i>typical</i>. So cheesy. So annoying. The guy's an asshole who more or less tells Natalie that he's glad her father's dead and she's all "but he's soooo hot". Give me a break, would ya?<br><br>I was reading this on my laptop in Adobe Digital Editions when my housemate came walking in and started reading the page I was on over my shoulder. She then began reading it out loud in a breathy voice and putting emphasis on certain words... well, how I wish I had recorded it and could put audio files in this review. What had been slowly getting more and more annoying to me finally hit breaking point when she voiced some of these ridiculous lines out loud. After hearing this spoken I decided I'd had enough:<br><br><i>He's changed out of his school uniform and is now wearing dark trousers, leather work boots and a fitted black shirt that <b>accentuates</b> every inch of his <b>powerful</b>, <b>muscular</b>, frame. He looks at me, <b>into me</b>, like he can see every secret I have, every rush of my blood. My pulse races with fear and a much more unexpected, disturbing emotion: <b>desire</b>. I turn away, horrified at my body's reaction to him. It's sick and irrational. He's a <b>darkling</b>, a predator that would gladly rip my throat out, given the slightest provocation. Then why are my cheeks burning so red? <b>I'm just hot from the fire, that's all.</b></i><br><br>Oh gawwwwddd. Really? Does everyone else have this problem that they can't tell the difference between genuine heat and horniness? Is no one else nauseated already by this same old "no, no, I mustn't, it's wrong" while the heroines are simultaneously fanning themselves with desire? I'm done with this silliness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3387720618661238208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_281408391" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281408391" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/281408391?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=stupid-girls">stupid-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=dont-understand-why-its-hyped">dont-understand-why-its-hyped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=unoriginal">unoriginal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=hot-mess">hot-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=why-do-people-like-this-shit">why-do-people-like-this-shit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer281408391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2183851665009252542">You know what I hate? I hate when I'm reading a book, and all I feel the whole time is anger, frustration and disappointment.<br/><br/>That's what I felt with <i>Black City</i>.<br/><br/>As you can see, this is yet another DNF review. Let me tell you why I disliked this book so much: the romance. You know how bad the romance was? It made me overlook everything else in the book; the world building, the other characters, the plot, all of it. The romance was just so bad that it drained my interest in the book more and more a</span>
  <span id="freeText2183851665009252542" style="display:none">You know what I hate? I hate when I'm reading a book, and all I feel the whole time is anger, frustration and disappointment.<br><br>That's what I felt with <i>Black City</i>.<br><br>As you can see, this is yet another DNF review. Let me tell you why I disliked this book so much: the romance. You know how bad the romance was? It made me overlook everything else in the book; the world building, the other characters, the plot, all of it. The romance was just so bad that it drained my interest in the book more and more as I read. Also, the FUCKING MADE UP SWEAR WORD! <i>Fragg</i>? Are you KIDDING ME? It sounds <i>ridiculous</i>.<br><br>The book is told from the points of views of our two protagonists, Natalie and Ash. Ash is a twin-blood Darkling (coughvampirecough) and Natalie is a Sentry, a human, and the daughter of the Emissary. I'll break down each of these two's chapters for you:<br><br><b>Ash's POV - first half of the book:</b> I hate that Sentry girl. Grr. Bitch stole my jacket. But my non-working heart flutters and beats when I see her and when she's around. But she's just a fragging Sentry! Who gives a fragg about her.<br><br><b>Natalie's POV - first half:</b> That Darkling boy, I can't get him out of my mind. But he's a Darkling! I shouldn't feel these feelings. But oh, his muscles... No! But I like his jacket, I'll keep it. It smells good.<br><br><b>Ash's POV - second half &amp; so forth:</b> I love her. She's my Blood Mate. Nothing will ever tear us apart. Natalie, Natalie, Natalie. But Evangeline is so hot... No, Natalie's my girlfriend! And my Blood Mate, my one true love. Natalie Natalie Natalie......<i>Evangeline</i>. NO! Natalie!<br><br><b>Natalie's POV - second half &amp; so forth:</b> Oh Ash, I love you so much. He's my one true love. I love him, and I don't care if what we have is forbidden. He's my Blood Mate and we'll never be apart, ever. Ash Ash Ash Ash Ash. He'll never hurt me, and he loves me too. Oh Ash... Ash Ash Ash.<br><br>Yeah.<br><br>Literally every paragraph in either of these two's chapters are about how hot and in love they are for each other. And they just say the most cheesiest things. -_- I lost interest in anything else about the book not only because the romance is bad, but because it's ALL THERE IS TO THE BOOK! It's so heavily based on the romance that I found it hard to focus on anything else because I'm constantly attacked by cheesy sentences left right and center. <br><br>The author also took the whole electric-touch thing to a whole nother level. There was one scene where they were making out and it was described as them feeling like...multiple <i>zaps</i> and shit. Why the fuck do all these characters in PNR/dystomance books like it when they feel zaps of electrity anyway? e_e That shit hurts. I wanna know who first started this ridiculous but annoyingly popular trend. It needs to die, and I know most of you agree with me on this.<br><br>And don't even get me started on the fucking cheating. Oh my god, this guy... Ash actually <i>cheats</i> on Natalie. We're treated to a steamy, detailed make-out scene of him with the Other Girl character, Evangeline, from his POV. And he was enjoying it. And he didn't even try to fight it. Natalie barged in a few minutes later, but could you imagine what would've happened if she didn't? I doubted it would have ended with just making out, because Ash really did get into it. I was so disgusted. I know some pretty asshole guys from other YA books, but none of them ever actually straight up <i>cheat</i> on the girl.<br><br>The author tried to pull out the "only-thinking-about-the-heroine-while-kissing-another-chick" card, too, with Ash going all: "<i>Only one name rang in my mind: Natalie.</i>" -_- Nice try, <i>Ash</i>. The H on your name should be changed into another S, is what I think.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380370416ra/723230.gif" height="200" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I stopped the book not long after that, because I just couldn't be bothered to continue. I mean, why should I? The romance was horrible and it clearly dominated the whole book, so much so that it made me not pay attention at all to the plot or the world-building.<br><br>Gah, I'm still so mad right now. This book definitely falls on the category of worst romances I've ever read. Cheesy crappy insta-love, and to top it all off the guy cheats on the girl! How worse can it get? I don't wanna stay around to find out. No thanks.<br><br>I know a lot of you are fans of this book, and you know, to each their own, but I personally just hated it for its ridiculous romance. So much so that it made me overlook everything else. If you guys still wanna give it a go, be my guest. Maybe the romance won't get to you as much as it did me.<br><br><b>Edit:</b> Yeah, as you can see, I repeat myself a <i>lot</i> in this review. ._. I guess I was just so angry lol. And it's just further proof of how infuriating and unbearable the romance in this book is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2183851665009252542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_392702260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392702260" />
    <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit"><img alt="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372018610p2/3854740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392702260?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit">Christina (Ensconced in Lit)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392702260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9150264854931051752">I have had several people approach me and say that this was one of the best ARCs they had read all year. So this has been high on my radar.<br/><br/>Black City by Elizabeth Richards may seem like an amalgam of familiar territory. We have vampires. We have a dystopian society. We have lovers on two different sides of a war. Sure, we start with the expected, and then Richards completely turns everything on its head. All I will say is that we have alternating perspectives of Natalie, the daughter of an Emiss</span>
  <span id="freeText9150264854931051752" style="display:none">I have had several people approach me and say that this was one of the best ARCs they had read all year. So this has been high on my radar.<br /><br />Black City by Elizabeth Richards may seem like an amalgam of familiar territory. We have vampires. We have a dystopian society. We have lovers on two different sides of a war. Sure, we start with the expected, and then Richards completely turns everything on its head. All I will say is that we have alternating perspectives of Natalie, the daughter of an Emissary, who is trying to keep Darklings segregated from Black City, and Ash, a Darkling, who sells Haze, a drug, to keep his family fed. These two unlikely kids seem to have a Romeo and Juliet kind of romance and then everything goes out the window. <br /><br />You must read this book. That's all I'm going to say. I don't want to give away any of the marvelous twists this book reveals, and I read the book from cover to cover in a day. The characters are terrific, and I love the dark setting of Black City. This isn't a perfect book, but it is an extremely compelling one. I know Richards is only going to get better and better with each installment.<br /><br />Overall, one of the most intriguing and pulse pounding dystopian books I've read this year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9150264854931051752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1784007641" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1784007641" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1784007641?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=help-help-i-m-being-repressed">help-help-i-m-being-repressed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784007641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer509732927075579074"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>One of the chief complaints about the YA genre - especially the books being targeted and marketed toward young women - is that they are becoming increasingly derivative, and seem to focus only on the romance. BLACK CITY is a perfect example of that: it's a book that can be neatly summed up by asking "what happens when you smush together DIVERGENT and TWILIGHT?"<br/><br/><br/><br/>I haven't given a one-star rating in a while, and to be honest - it feels weir</span>
  <span id="freeText509732927075579074" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>One of the chief complaints about the YA genre - especially the books being targeted and marketed toward young women - is that they are becoming increasingly derivative, and seem to focus only on the romance. BLACK CITY is a perfect example of that: it's a book that can be neatly summed up by asking "what happens when you smush together DIVERGENT and TWILIGHT?"<br><br><br><br>I haven't given a one-star rating in a while, and to be honest - it feels weird. It's been so <i>long </i>since I read a book that I thought was bad, that I forgot what the actual experience was like. The incredulity. The frustration. The boredom. What really annoyed me was how much I <i>wanted </i>to like BLACK CITY in the first place, because vampires are awesome, and a dystopian society involving vampires should also be awesome, because <i>vampires</i> and <i>oppression</i>. Plus, that cover. That's a cover to take home to mama.<br><br><br><br>The problem starts with the world-building. The author employs a lot of really clunky terminology, like "Darklings" for vampires, "twin-bloods" for half-breeds, "Sight" for vampiric thralls, and "the v-gene" for...a special gene that lets you 'sense' vampires, I guess. There's also different classes of vampires, with different colored hair and eyes, and some have wings, and then there's this degenerative necrosis-inducing disease that only affects vampires that's called Wrath, which makes their skin rot away. Got all that? But wait, there's <i>more - </i><br><br><br><br>They call the trance-like state humans go into "Haze", which is confusing because Haze can also be sold in a bottle in drug form, and sometimes it is especially potent, which is called Golden Haze. And then there's these creatures called "Bastets" which appear to be shape-shifter leopards who have venom in their teeth. Trackers hunt the Darklings after curfew, protecting the Sentry, or the ruling government class, from Workboots (the poor) and the Legion (vampire revolutionaries). Violating the various laws that are in place to fraternize with a Darkling makes you a "race traitor."<br><br><br><br>The world all of this terms are used in isn't much clearer. I think it's supposed to be an alternate version of our world, except for some reason all of the states in the U.S. have been split into nine megastates with lame names like "Emerald State", but it's never really explained. Also, why are we a fascist, cultish dictatorship with a fascist, cultish leader? What happened? <i>I </i>never voted for this guy!<br><br><br><br>By the end of the book, I mostly had a handle on all the terminology, although I was still eying the world skeptically (what happened to the rest of the world? This is exactly what happened in DIVERGENT - Future Chicago went to heck in a hand basket, but was that an isolated incident? A reality TV show that the rest of the world just watched in amusement while shaking their head and going, "Oh, Chicago, you silly little cinnamon rolls, what <i>will </i>you think of next?") Also, why are the vampires allowing this to happen in the first place? They have literal "opium dens" for the Haze users. If their strength and their wings failed them, it wouldn't take much effort to just get all the humans hooked on Haze for a hostile takeover. But I might still have been able to enjoy the book in spite of all these plot holes and vocabulary words if it weren't for the two main characters - Ash and Natalie. Ash is a twin-blood (half-breed) and Natalie is a Sentry (ruling class). Twin-bloods don't have beating hearts for some reason (they're vestigial, I guess), but when Natalie touches him on accident - <i>his heart actually starts beating</i> because, and I kid you not, she's his <i>soul mate</i>, and your heart only beats as a twin-blood once you find the One.<br><br><br><br><div>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1381683023i/5184659.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</div><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>They talk about how special and unique their love is before they've even really exchanged much more than a few paragraphs of conversation and by the time that they agree to go out with each other, before they've even gone on a single date, they're already ready to sacrifice all of their friendships and family ties and even their <i>lives </i>for each other. Even Romeo and Juliet would be side-eying these two. They're also just not very nice characters. Natalie is especially helpless, biting her lip, blushing, and staring in horror whenever something unpleasant happens. She tries to brush all of the bad things under the carpet, including the horrible acts that her mother and father have done to the vampires. Ash isn't much better. He helps get his "best friend" hooked on drugs and does some pretty sketchy things to women who aren't Natalie. It's hard to root for characters you don't like - particularly when you know that you <i>are </i>supposed to like those characters, and relate to them, and see yourself in them.<br><br><br><br>I do own the sequel to this book, BLACK PHOENIX, which I will be reading soon. I'd like to see if the author improves over time, and is capable of doing that lovely, lovely cover justice. There were some things in this book I didn't expect, but they were minor plot twists and overshadowed by the epically unconvincing love story. I can understand why so many reviewers were disappointed by BLACK CITY. I was, too.<br><br><br><br><b>1 star.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="509732927075579074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_455601783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/455601783" />
    <a title="Belle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9419782-belle"><img alt="Belle" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/455601783?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Belle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Belle" href="/user/show/9419782-belle">Belle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=hero-saves-the-day">hero-saves-the-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=kickass-heroines">kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=heavy-drama">heavy-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=heartache">heartache</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9419782-belle?shelf=hot-leading-men">hot-leading-men</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer455601783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13831124670397683954"><b> SOME SPOILERS! </b><br/><br/>WTF DID I JUST READ.<br/><br/>HOLY SHIT.<br/><br/>My first thought post this book.. is a) i want to marry Ash<br/>but then I think harder so b) WHY did I not read this as soon as I got it ! Rookie error Belinda, Rookie, Rookie error.<br/><br/>This book was amazing. It was a whole lot of loving and more. <br/><br/><b>The Characters </b><br/><i>Ash:</i> He is like the epitome of any leading man you could ever want in your life. He knows when to be a smart ass, irresistible and cocky.. but knows when to be caring, kind and compassionate to other</span>
  <span id="freeText13831124670397683954" style="display:none"><b> SOME SPOILERS! </b><br /><br />WTF DID I JUST READ.<br /><br />HOLY SHIT.<br /><br />My first thought post this book.. is a) i want to marry Ash<br />but then I think harder so b) WHY did I not read this as soon as I got it ! Rookie error Belinda, Rookie, Rookie error.<br /><br />This book was amazing. It was a whole lot of loving and more. <br /><br /><b>The Characters </b><br /><i>Ash:</i> He is like the epitome of any leading man you could ever want in your life. He knows when to be a smart ass, irresistible and cocky.. but knows when to be caring, kind and compassionate to others. His vulnerability about not feeling like he belonged to either Darkling or human side. His feelings of abandonment by his mother, his vulnerability, his love for Natalie, his joy and confusion over his heart beating. Man, where do they make boys like him.. if anyone knows <u> SIGN ME UP ! </u><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Although I won't lie when he kissed Evangeline - I mean yeah i get he was confused and trying to sort his feelings out - I was seriously going to bitchslap him through the pages. Glad, he made the right decision and sorted his shit out.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br /><i>Natalie:</i> Her character definitely grew on me. I was a bit hesitant at first because I could tell how conflicted she was when seeing the torturing and oppression of the Darklings, but at the same time did nothing. However, as the book grew, her strength grew and consequently my love for her character definitely grew. She became the kick ass heroine I knew she could be. The way she gave Ash her complete heart was so admirable, and how she cared for Sebastian even though he wronged her. Damn woman you are too nice for your own good. <br /><br /><i>Sebastian:</i> When his character first got introduced I was like.. oh no here comes the love triangle. But boy was I pleasantly surprised that it didnt end up that way. In fact for the majority of the story he is public enemy number one. Sure at times I thought he had some good qualities sometimes.. but.. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[After the attempted rape.. no redemption can come out of his character for me. I mean I was going to give you a last chance, but seriously it's a hell no from me. DIE DIE DIE  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>Beetle/ Day: </i>Yeah LOVE these characters. I won't lie both of them at times got under my skin. What with Beetle being a nincompoop over hazing (otherwise known as drugs in this world) and with Day being a stubborn cow. Although I wont lie I am pretty stubborn so it is like a pot calling the kettle black. But when they got their crap together i love the two of them ! They are a match made in heaven, and supporting characters/great friends to both the leads :) !<br /><br /><i> Evangaline:</i> Now I won't lie to you and say I didnt want to kick her ass to Timbuktu throughout the majority of the book. Simply because no one steals my man except Natalie. But then as I write this, guilty, nagging thoughts are rising from the back of my mind.. of sympathy. I mean wouldn't it just suck a lot to watch someone you love with some one else. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean how sad would it be, to realise the one person you are meant to be with has already found a blood mate and is in love with someone else because she has your heart. That would kill me. How unfair would you think life is. And the fact that she is a carrier so won't really be able to find someone else to love.. damn. BUT that spoiler being said, Im glad Ash tried to make her realise that the heart/ blood bond was purely superficial whereas the love he shares with Natalie runs deeper.. they are soulmates. Hopefully she will find happiness in another character  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I hope she gets what she deserves next book.<br /><br /><b>The Backstory </b><br />Wow, what an amazing back drop this book was cast in. I mean the world of this book.. is intriguing, mysterious, completely realistic for a make believe world and makes you feel like you are within the pages of this book living in this fantasy. Although of course I wouldnt be that keen to live there if I was a darkling. I wont lie, I was a bit uncertain with the whole the vampires/Darklings are the outcasts and rejects, while the humans are the power race. That seemed pretty unrealistic, but after reasons were given it started to make more sense to me. The way Richards has really thought out and given us such a supreme knowledge of the world in which her characters live in only further enhances the storyline of this book. I can not wait to read the next book in this series.<br /><br /><b>The Plot </b><br />I won't lie, I love anything to do with civil rights movements and this book was no different. Sure it was in a made up world where vampires roamed but it really connected with me due to the messages it sent out. The way in which humans oppressed, murdered and treated the Darklings like dirt was intriguing to read. The wristbands that they had to wear reminds me of the Jews in World War 2 or the passbooks in the Civil Rights movement in America. It really reflects real life this book. I loved the rebellious spirit of the citizens who refused to watch the hangings, and all those who rose up against the injustices. I loved how ignorance soon turned into awareness and action in this book. <br /><br />THIS BOOK WAS AMAZING! i give it a solid 5/5!! Can't gush about it's awesomeness enough. Read read read this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13831124670397683954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan" href="/user/show/5327905-morgan">Morgan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5327905-morgan?shelf=won-from-giveaway">won-from-giveaway</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer428955157&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428955157" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9004967047181945246">Review of <i> Black City </i>, written by Elizabeth Richards.<br/>Won from a giveaway via Goodreads.com<br/>Expected Publication: 11/13/12<br/><br/>My Overall Rating: One Star<br/>Cover Rating: 4 Stars - gorgeous, though slightly similar to the <i> Twilight </i> cover theme, if you know what I mean.<br/><br/>What I knew about this book before beginning it:<br/>1. Vampires. (Or, Darklings, as they're called in this book.)<br/>2. Dystopia setting, of course.<br/>3. Romance. Duh. It's YA with vampires in a dystopian setting.<br/>4. The main character's name is Ash. </span>
  <span id="freeText9004967047181945246" style="display:none">Review of <i> Black City </i>, written by Elizabeth Richards.<br />Won from a giveaway via Goodreads.com<br />Expected Publication: 11/13/12<br /><br />My Overall Rating: One Star<br />Cover Rating: 4 Stars - gorgeous, though slightly similar to the <i> Twilight </i> cover theme, if you know what I mean.<br /><br />What I knew about this book before beginning it:<br />1. Vampires. (Or, Darklings, as they're called in this book.)<br />2. Dystopia setting, of course.<br />3. Romance. Duh. It's YA with vampires in a dystopian setting.<br />4. The main character's name is Ash. While not terribly original (considering he's a vampire and that's a slightly vampire-y name)it's not as terrible as it could be.<br />5. Two narrators.... <br /><br />Review:<br />Alright. I have a lot to say, and most of it isn't all that great... at all. Granted, there are some good things... but the majority of it... sigh.<br /><br />Okay, let's get started with the good stuff:<br /><br />1. I actually started to genuinely enjoy this book within the last 10 chapters or so. Things were <i> actually </i> happening. I was surprised by a couple of things. But then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ash came back from the dead 'cause ohmyGodhe'sJesusnow  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and I went back to rolling my eyes and waiting for the "fragging" book to be over with.<br /><br />2. I also liked some of the world building. Black City was an interesting enough place, with the Wall and the Legion and the Rise, etc, etc. <br /><br />3. Evangeline. Yeah, I liked her. Her part in the story was genuinely interesting.<br />Other than these couple of things, there just wasn't anything about this book that I loved... or even <i> liked, </i> really.<br /><br />Onto the bad stuff:<br /><br />1. This story was painfully unoriginal. I mean, there was a load of stuff that was similar to either Harry Potter <br /><br /><i> "Gregory stretches out a hand to Natalie.<br />'I'm Gregory Thompson,' he says. 'My father works for the Department of Subspecies Management, sorts out the Synth-O-Blood shipments to the Legion, that sort of thing. Ever heard of him?'<br />Natalie smiles politely. 'The name doesn't ring a bell.'<br />He looks disappointed. 'Well, it's an honor to have you here. I'll happily show you around the school-'<br />'Day's doing that, but thanks,' she says dismissively. </i><br />Waaiiit for iiiit:<br /><i> "'You don't want to be seen with </i> her <i> sort, she's one of the Rise kids,' he says to Natalie. 'I'll set you up with the right type of people to know.'<br />Day's cheeks burn red.<br />'I can make my own mind up about who the 'right type of people' are,' Natalie snaps.'I'm already getting a pretty good idea of who I want to avoid.'" </i><br /><br />or Twilight (for obvious reasons)or some other vampire/YA/dystopian cliche.<br /><br />2. The characters. My God, there wasn't a single character that I even remotely liked. Not one. Seriously! (Not even Evangeline. Yes, she was interesting, but I still didn't like her.) Natalie was annoying, Ash was annoying, Day overreacted about everything (so did everyone, really), and Beetle was lame. And a druggie. And pathetically in love with Day.<br />Also, there was absolutely NO character development (aside from Natalie being all Miss Priss I'm-So-Rich in, like, the second chapter to being all omgiloveeveryoneequallyexceptformymother!).<br /><br />3. The use of the word "fragging" and the <i> italics that were everywhere. </i><br />"Fragg"? Seriously?! Nobody says that! Ever!<br />Also, don't even get me started on those italics. There were completely unnecessary! The story was told in the first person. We were able to read their thoughts. They didn't need to be italicized randomly, whenever you felt like it, Elizabeth! Graaaahhhh!<br /><br />Okay, moving on.<br /><br />4. The romance. Oh, the romance. <br />First off, they met within the first chapter or so. Boring. Also, there was electricity when they touched. How original. Guess what else? Their hearts fluttered/tugged/jumped/skydived/blah blah blah. Natalie had a heart condition, for God's sake! Hon, if you are on heart meds and you're supposed to tell your doctor if you're heart if being all janked up, why the <i> hell </i> would you think your heart "tugging" is not a reason for concern?!<br />GRAH.<br /><br />5. Poor pacing. Nothing big really happened until the last few chapters.<br /><br />That's about all I can say, without going into extreme detail, but I think you get the point. Overall, the book was unoriginal, cliched, and (aside from a few scenes toward the end) just <i> bad </i>.<br />At one point, I just stopped reading it for a week because I couldn't bring myself to read it.<br /><br />Please don't go out and read it. It's just not worth it.</span>

<div id="review_272862712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272862712" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1928123-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586906845p2/1928123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272862712?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/1928123-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1928123-katie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1928123-katie?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272862712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1476061599399509813">The dystopian trend seems to be getting a bit old. All the books have a similar feel to them and the stories are becoming less unique. That is not at all the case with Black City. Elizabeth Richards has created a world all her own with fantastic history, unbelievable creatures, and a bleak setting that manages to stand out against all others.<br/><br/>Black City is a place in ruins. Ash still rains down from bombs that were set off a year ago. Buildings crumble daily and no new ones are built to replace t</span>
  <span id="freeText1476061599399509813" style="display:none">The dystopian trend seems to be getting a bit old. All the books have a similar feel to them and the stories are becoming less unique. That is not at all the case with Black City. Elizabeth Richards has created a world all her own with fantastic history, unbelievable creatures, and a bleak setting that manages to stand out against all others.<br /><br />Black City is a place in ruins. Ash still rains down from bombs that were set off a year ago. Buildings crumble daily and no new ones are built to replace them. People live in the rubble but fear speaking out to get better living conditions. In the middle of it all is a walled enclosure where all the Darklings are forced to live. However, things may not be that way for long. The Darklings are unhappy with their restrictions and they are ready to fight. Black City is a city on the brink of war.<br /><br />Ash is a twin-blood. He is half human, half Darkling. He lives outside the Darkling enclosure but he does not feel accepted. He is lonely and sad and it causes him to do some stupid things. However, it is easy to tell that he is a good guy at heart. Readers will definitely fall for this dark and lonely guy. Natalie is also alone but that is because of her station. She is the Emissary's daughter and most people are afraid she could get them in trouble. Even though she is lonely she is friendly and caring and very easy to like. She's smart, brave, and loyal. What's not to like? Beethe and Day are also fabulous. Beethe is hilarious. He's kind of a druggie but he's a sweetheart and he's trying to change his ways. Day is smart (sometimes too smart), kind, yet she can be hard-headed. She makes some mistakes but she learns from them.<br /><br />Elizabeth Richards really knows how to create a terrifying villain. Sebastian, Gregory, Natalie's mom, and Purian Rose are all completely evil. Natalie's mom is manipulative and sick. Sebastian tries to hide his dark side but it definitely does not work. Gregory doesn't try to hide his prejudice and nastiness. Purian Rose is by far the worst though. He is the leader of church and state. He hides his evilness by saying it's "His mighty's" will. He is cruel and sick. I both dread and look forward to reading more about him.<br /><br />The plot focuses quite a bit on the forbidden romance between Ash and Natalie but that is definitely not all that is going on (although that part was great.) Because of Ash, Natalie discovers a lot about Darklings and a lot about her family. Ash discovers that people can't be judged based on their parents. There is also quite a bit of mystery that will have readers hooked. <br /><br />Overall, Black City is a favorite of mine that I must recommend. Dystopian fans HAVE to read this one. And romance fans because it is one steamy romance. Really everyone should just read it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1476061599399509813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_286152805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286152805" />
    <a title="Taschima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima"><img alt="Taschima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574541558p2/2435020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286152805?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taschima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taschima" href="/user/show/2435020-taschima">Taschima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286152805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3840422140686103199">You can find more reviews <a href='http://bloodybookaholic.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@BloodyBookaholic</a><br/><br/>To put it in the simplest terms <b>Black City</b> is like <b>Legend</b> only mixed with vampires. This is not a bad thing; <b>Legend</b> is great, and so is <b>Black City</b>! It has some of the things <b>Legend</b> has, only heightened- ex. love becomes forbidden love. Corrupt government? Check. People being oppressed? Check. Two main characters, one from the government the other a normal person? Check. Adding to this delight <b>Black City</b> manages to have a plot that is original and not mo</span>
  <span id="freeText3840422140686103199" style="display:none">You can find more reviews <a href="http://bloodybookaholic.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">@BloodyBookaholic</a><br /><br />To put it in the simplest terms <b>Black City</b> is like <b>Legend</b> only mixed with vampires. This is not a bad thing; <b>Legend</b> is great, and so is <b>Black City</b>! It has some of the things <b>Legend</b> has, only heightened- ex. love becomes forbidden love. Corrupt government? Check. People being oppressed? Check. Two main characters, one from the government the other a normal person? Check. Adding to this delight <b>Black City</b> manages to have a plot that is original and not monotonous. <b>Black City</b> is that typical book you can't put down, it enthralls you with it's very complicated dark world,it makes your heart beat just a little bit faster. I bet If you were a half-darkling this book would kick start your heart right up.<br /><br />It is a hot day in Black City (I can only imagine) when Natalie, the Emmisary's daughter (fancy term for a high ranking government official), and her remaining family move to the crappiest place in the world, Black City, from Centrum (a "better" city than Black City). On top of that she now has to attend public school along with the rest of the work boots (not so fancy term for people who actually have to work for a living). How will she ever survive?<br /><br /><i>"It's your bew identity bracelet. Do you like it?" I ask.<br /><br />Martha nods slighly, not saying anything. She must be overwhelmed; it's a very expensive gift. She slips it on.</i><br /><br />Some context on the quote, Martha is Natalie's maid and she is a Darkling (Darklings who live on the human side of the wall are made to use bracelets with their info on them). I thought this quote described Natalie great at the beginning of the novel. Natalie pissed me off at first. She was such a spoiled brat. It was hard to root for her, but then she grows up. It's so amazing, she went from someone who I wouldn't touch with a ten foot pole to a brave self sufficient heroine that doesn't need to be rescued. I respect her, I like her.<br /><br /><i>"I place a hand against the wall and slip my other hand between her thighs, gently easing her legs apart. Touching her doesn't turn me on, but I groan like it does, knowing she'll enjoy that. They all do, even the guys -it's why they come to me instead of the Haze dens."</i><br /><br />Ash is a Haze dealer, and a half-Darkling. You can say he got the "short" end of the stick in life (though in fact he is really tall). He is an outcast, abondoned by his mother at a young age. It's clear that he has issues.But It is very hard NOT to like Ash, he is so conflicted. You just want to hug him, and help him. <i>He</i> is the one who drew me to the story beginning on Chapter 1.<br /><br />The story evolves around these two characters with a backdrop of war, corruption, and danger. It's a very dark world, but then again which dystopian world isn't?<br /><br />The characters, the world building, the intense connection between the characters, the customs of Black City and the Darklings, all of this and more is what I loved about this book. It was just a very good read.<br /><br />Some things were hard for me to swallow, like how can the vampires (who are stronger, faster, PREDATORS) be oppressed by the humans? I would have liked some more information on the old war. What happened, and how? Were the humans always privy to the existence of this other race? How did they exactly beat the vampires and made them live in guettos? I have no idea! I missed that history lesson.<br /><br />Another thing that bothered me was the romance, at first. Because the characters show this instant connection to each other without really knowing anything about each other. They meet, they dislike/are sttracted to each other, and on the next page they are bound together. This was something that bothered me, BUT it was completely addrssed and insta-love was succesfully avoided. And even though I could smell the twist to the romance a mile away I still enjoyed it (maybe I like being proved right).<br /><br />But if you can look past the non existent/much needed history lesson you will really enjoy this novel. I liked the writing, I loved Ash, and I liked Natalie, as well as the rest of the characters. It's a very easy story to get sunk into, and I enjoyed every single page.<br /><br />**Quotes taken from an ARC copy, subject to change.</span>

<div id="review_1952879890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952879890" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1952879890?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1952879890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12209715551851504492">1.7 stars, this book and its male and female leads remind me often of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658-legend?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Legend</i>
</a> by Marie Lu, <b>and I'm not saying it in a good way</b>.<br/><br/>So, in what way <i>Black City</i> is similar with Legend? Let's do a check list.<br/><br/><b>(1) Vague and poorly constructed dyspotian world:</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515915213ra/24873874.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(Link: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://giphy.com/gifs/dystopian-8qat33Q57Uf0Q'>https://giphy.com/gifs/dystopian-8qat...</a>)<br/><br/>Dystopia, you said?<br/><br/><br/>We never know what is going on with the rest of the world or why this fictional world had become what it is today. We only see the events that happen within one city, we only know t</span>
  <span id="freeText12209715551851504492" style="display:none">1.7 stars, this book and its male and female leads remind me often of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658-legend?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Legend</i>
</a> by Marie Lu, <b>and I'm not saying it in a good way</b>.<br><br>So, in what way <i>Black City</i> is similar with Legend? Let's do a check list.<br><br><b>(1) Vague and poorly constructed dyspotian world:</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515915213ra/24873874.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://giphy.com/gifs/dystopian-8qat33Q57Uf0Q">https://giphy.com/gifs/dystopian-8qat...</a>)<br><br>Dystopia, you said?<br><br><br>We never know what is going on with the rest of the world or why this fictional world had become what it is today. We only see the events that happen within one city, we only know there is a deadly plague haunting the population and....you guessed it...we also have an evil government and an evil, power-crazed state leader/dictator. Only that in Black City, we get a humanoid specie known as 'The Darklings' (X-Men? Vampires? What are they actually? I don't know.)<br><br>Not to mention, in Black City, despite of the evil, mean government and the power crazed dictator (who has been enjoying a fiery cult following and be viewed by his followers as a holy man), said evil government still allows its citizens to each have a vote to decide whether they should pass a law to crush down on the suppressed Darklings.<br><br>Seriously?<br><br><b>(2) A supposed streetwise male lead from a humble background and a main girl who is from a rich and privileged family:</b> <br><br>*sighs* It's just the same old, same old 'I'm a poor boy but she is from a rich family' YA romance angst bullshit.<br><br><b>(3) The heroine has an asshole suitor/ex boyfriend who is in the army:</b><br><br>And the jerk is following her around in the name of 'I'm protecting you from harm', plus he also <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ had gone after the heroine's older sibling first before shifting attention to her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><br><b>(4) The male lead is a poorly written 'reluctant hero':</b><br><br>In Black City, the male lead's best buddy wants to join a protest <b>which aims at protecting the rights of the male lead and his fellow Darklings</b> (the male lead himself is a half-human, half-Darkling hybird). Naturally this best friend wants the male lead to join in the protest as well, but guess what is his reaction?<br><br>His reaction: 'You will only get yourself killed.'<br><br>So...this male lead wants to stay out of trouble and save his own hide, which is fine, but guess who has eventually become a hero in the eyes of the citizens? Who? The best friend or the male lead? Who?<br><br><b>(5) By the end everyone becomes drama queen:</b><br><br>When there is an evil government's conspiracy going on, the lives of many Darklings and general citizens are at stake, and a bloody battle between the evil government and the rebels is well underway, our main couple still decide to care more about their love life than what is going on outside of their relationship.<br><br>And you don't even want to know how the huge crisis is averted in the very end. I rolled my eyes at how the MCs act like a bunch of drama queens when the evil government is closing in on them, these people should have long been killed when their every reaction is based on impulse and anger instead of carefulness and self-control. I mean, when facing a suppressing, ruthless government, people should act with careful measure, not just open your mouth and speak whatever you want and react out of anger, right?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515914638ra/24873828.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://giphy.com/gifs/sherlock-john-watson-drama-queen-5AN3sz5GBC55m">https://giphy.com/gifs/sherlock-john-...</a>)<br><br><b>(6) Last but not least...the YA romance angst and insta-love</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515914638ra/24873829.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://giphy.com/gifs/thg-BgltgOWHsJq0w">https://giphy.com/gifs/thg-BgltgOWHsJq0w</a>)<br><br>Let me tell you this...the heart is only an organ which helps us to pump blood all over our bodies, it has nothing to do with our romantic feeling and love life.<br><br>But according to Elizabeth Richards it is not the case with the male lead and the Darklings! Due to some reason, their hearts never beat until they found their ONE TRUE LOVE!!!!!<br><br>Why would they be like this? You know...reasons!<br><br>Okay...the Immortal After Dark series has similar setting and I never like it, but at least the idea doesn't sound as stupid in the IAD series.<br><br>Not just this, but the male and female leads also start proclaiming their true love to each other shortly after they meet and chat with each other for least than ten times.<br><br>*facepalms*<br><br>To be honest, the extra 0.7 star is for the plot twist in the end. These few plot twists are actually quite creative, but the rest of the book...*sighs*<br><br>The Final Words: if you happened to have a lot of time to waste, read this book.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12209715551851504492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_643129395" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/643129395" />
    <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland"><img alt="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417030210p2/5749698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/643129395?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland">Kat (Lost in Neverland)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of ridiculous paranormal YA romance and don't mind plagarism</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=lust-and-love-are-not-the-same">lust-and-love-are-not-the-same</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=le-sigh">le-sigh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=stupid-heroine">stupid-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=watch-for-flying-tables-everybody">watch-for-flying-tables-everybody</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=cheesy-romance">cheesy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer643129395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7656061066170092770"><br/>Ash is a twin-blood Darkling, a half human creature that drinks blood to survive. In the Black City, Darklings are relentlessly hunted and persecuted, most of which are kept behind a massive wall splitting the Darklings from the humans. <br/>Natalie is the daughter of the Sentry, one of the most powerful women in the city and working to remove the Darklings permanently. <br/>Ash and Natalie meet one night briefly, and to Ash's shock, his normally dead-silent chest starts to thrum with a heartbeat. <br/><br/><br/>Wow. I </span>
  <span id="freeText7656061066170092770" style="display:none"><br>Ash is a twin-blood Darkling, a half human creature that drinks blood to survive. In the Black City, Darklings are relentlessly hunted and persecuted, most of which are kept behind a massive wall splitting the Darklings from the humans. <br>Natalie is the daughter of the Sentry, one of the most powerful women in the city and working to remove the Darklings permanently. <br>Ash and Natalie meet one night briefly, and to Ash's shock, his normally dead-silent chest starts to thrum with a heartbeat. <br><br><br>Wow. I should have known; this book was one of the 'Breathless Reads', along with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13455112.Origin" title="Origin by Jessica Khoury" rel="nofollow noopener">Origin</a>, which I hated with a passion. <br><br>Imagine <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658.Legend__Legend___1_" title="Legend (Legend, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a> mashed together with Romeo and Juliet, and bits and pieces from other books like Harry Potter, and you got Black City.<br><br>Unlike <i>Legend</i>, this is not 'love'. These two know each other for a couple weeks before they start throwing around words like 'love' and 'Blood Mate' (which is how Darklings know who to mate). Ash and Natalie have no chemistry whatsoever besides physical attractions. The story could have been a very neat fascinating book had it not focused wholly on the relationship bullshit. <br>It is your typical YA paranormal lust-fest. Not much new here. What bothers me is that the story had real potential. <br>Despite their rather ridiculous similarities to other supernatural beings, the Darklings were interesting and I wanted to know more about them. The Bastets, enemy of the Darklings, were catlike creatures that were sparsely mentioned, but I wanted to learn more about that 'species' as well. Of course, the story only manages to focus on Ash and Natalie's 'romance'. <br><br><br>So let me clear this up;<br><br>A Darkling is basically a glorified vampire, mixed with a Time Lord. <br><u>Vampire abilities</u>: Fangs, needs blood to survive, 'tall and pale'. <br><u>Time Lord abilities</u>: Two hearts, regenerating cells that make them difficult to kill. <br><br>Not to mention they howl like werewolves and some species have wings like fairies. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/679192.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>It seems to me that Richards just put a bunch of supernatural creatures in a blender and called the resulting goop a 'Darkling'. <br><br>The world of the Black City was simply a fucked up version of our world going backwards in time. Women wore corsets, there were public floggings and executions, religion was a rising power, books were banned, etc. Oh, and instead of guns, officers and Trackers used swords.<br><br>FUCKING SWORDS.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425634ra/849617.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This ain't the 15th century, people. Although, apparently, it was in this world.<br><br>Characters?<br><br>Eh, Natalie was a baby who had brief moments of coolness, Ash was an ass mostly who had brief moments of cuteness. I liked Day. <br>They hardly ever go into family matters until the end when the plot demands it. <br>The writing was mediocre at best, couldn't care less for the characters, it was just overall kind of stupid. There were a few parts I liked but the writing had no depth or life to it so it brought down the story a bit. Yet another book to die miserably from the effects of teen romance! It was doomed from the start, honestly, with that kind of first chapter and description. <br>I honestly don't know what made me want to read this. Never pick up books where the first sentence of the description has 'they fell in love' in it. <br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7656061066170092770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Eyehavenofilter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7577191-eyehavenofilter"><img alt="Eyehavenofilter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387541295p2/7577191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421275847?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eyehavenofilter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eyehavenofilter" href="/user/show/7577191-eyehavenofilter">Eyehavenofilter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7577191-eyehavenofilter?shelf=other-worlds">other-worlds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7577191-eyehavenofilter?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7577191-eyehavenofilter?shelf=time-i-will-never-get-back">time-i-will-never-get-back</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7577191-eyehavenofilter?shelf=vampire">vampire</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421275847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15380325163642068704"> Hmmm what do I say about this? In the very very beginning I thought I was going to like this a lot, it had some very interesting qualities. Bad Vampire boy, goody goody girl, jealous girlfriend and jealous ex-boyfriend, drugs, vampires,(who are called unaffectionately " nipper" ( I didn't get the joke for about 4 chapters) all different breeds of them, and laws that were out of control, not unlike communist Russia in the 1940's , it seemed like it was going to be my kind of book. But it wasn't.</span>
  <span id="freeText15380325163642068704" style="display:none"> Hmmm what do I say about this? In the very very beginning I thought I was going to like this a lot, it had some very interesting qualities. Bad Vampire boy, goody goody girl, jealous girlfriend and jealous ex-boyfriend, drugs, vampires,(who are called unaffectionately " nipper" ( I didn't get the joke for about 4 chapters) all different breeds of them, and laws that were out of control, not unlike communist Russia in the 1940's , it seemed like it was going to be my kind of book. But it wasn't... It was dreadful. It dragged, it almost plagiarized, it took right turns then fell backwards.<br /> Then, it went haywire. And when I say haywire I mean "razor wire crazy" hints of trains to an "Auschwitz" type camp for infected Vampires, on the outskirts of nowhere, intown ghettos for Vampires, complete with a "Berlin Wall"!<br /> Crucifixions, as a means of public execution, Vampire race wars, laws against interracial marriages with Vampires or "Darklings" ( which for some unknown reason I kept reading as "ducklings" for about 10 pages),must be my dyslexia....an all powerful leader that has secret testings going on unbeknownst to the general public,(?) and harvesting body parts, I could go on and on but I wont, because....I just can't catch my breath.....<br /> Oh, there's more, much, much more, but if I put it all down, you wouldn't believe me. <br />I think if this had been split up into about 3 or 4 books....maybe I could have taken this far fetched stuff and digested it slowly! ( NOT) but all this and in ONE book? Good grief!<br />I mean seriously? I hope there isn't a book 2 or 3! There's no where else to go!<br />I feel badly that I didn't like this book as much as I wanted to.... It had promise.... Like some guys I've dated, but left me unfulfilled ( same as above!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15380325163642068704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1909418675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909418675" />
    <a title=" ☯Meera☯" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43209152-meera"><img alt=" ☯Meera☯" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520780809p2/43209152.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1909418675?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ☯Meera☯" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ☯Meera☯" href="/user/show/43209152-meera"> ☯Meera☯</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1909418675" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3655691357386391348">Why was this book ever published? <br/>It was terrible, it was absolutely horrific.<br/>Honestly, it was just eye-rolling, tacky-romance, flimsy-character, terrible-writing, <i>terrible</i>. Like, who even authorized this book?<br/><br/>First of all, it was like insta-romance. "Omg, a DARKLING! Must resist!"<br/><br/>I couldn't even FINISH it. What I read sums up to this:<br/><br/>Ash: I don't deserve to be loved. I am super broody and really hostile and a total jerk. But I've got my reasons.<br/><br/>Natalie: This boy intrigues me.
